<td class="nowrap" style="vertical-align:middle; border:none; padding:0.08em;"><p style="margin:0pt;"><b>(<span class="reference nourlexpansion" id="math_2" style="font-weight:bold; font-style:italic;">2</span>)</b></p>
</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>
<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle A}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>A</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle A}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="A" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7daff47fa58cdfd29dc333def748ff5fa4c923e3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.743ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle B}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>B</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle B}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="B" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/47136aad860d145f75f3eed3022df827cee94d7a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.764ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> are constants fit from data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bird2007_p29-31_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bird2007_p29-31-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> One the other hand, several authors express caution with respect to this model.
Errors as large as 30% can be encountered using equation (<b><a href="#math_1">1</a></b>), compared with fitting equation (<b><a href="#math_2">2</a></b>) to experimental data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bird2007_p29-31_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-Bird2007_p29-31-34">[34]</a></sup> More fundamentally, the physical assumptions underlying equation (<b><a href="#math_1">1</a></b>) have been extensively criticized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hildebrand1958_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hildebrand1958-36">[36]</a></sup> It has also been argued that the exponential dependence in equation (<b><a href="#math_1">1</a></b>) does not necessarily describe experimental observations more accurately than simpler, non-exponential expressions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Egelstaff1992_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Egelstaff1992-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>In light of these shortcomings, the development of a less ad-hoc model is a matter of practical interest.
Foregoing simplicity in favor of precision, it is possible to write rigorous expressions for viscosity starting from the fundamental equations of motion for molecules. A classic example 
of this approach is Irving-Kirkwood theory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Irving1949_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Irving1949-39">[39]</a></sup> On the other hand, such expressions
are given as averages over multiparticle <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Correlation_functions" title="Correlation functions">correlation functions</a> and are therefore difficult to apply in practice. 
</p><p>In general, empirically derived expressions (based on existing viscosity measurements) appear to be the only consistently reliable means of calculating viscosity in liquids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Selected_substances">Selected substances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Viscosity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Selected substances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Viscosity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Air_dry_dynamic_visocity_on_pressure_temperature.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="382" data-file-width="518" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Air_dry_dynamic_visocity_on_pressure_temperature.svg/220px-Air_dry_dynamic_visocity_on_pressure_temperature.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Air_dry_dynamic_visocity_on_pressure_temperature.svg/330px-Air_dry_dynamic_visocity_on_pressure_temperature.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Air_dry_dynamic_visocity_on_pressure_temperature.svg/440px-Air_dry_dynamic_visocity_on_pressure_temperature.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Air_dry_dynamic_visocity_on_pressure_temperature.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pressure dependence of the dynamic viscosity of dry air at the temperatures of 300, 400 and 500 kelvins</div></div></div>
<p>The viscosity of air depends mostly on the temperature. At 15 °C, the viscosity of air is <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">6995181000000000000♠</span>1.81<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>−5</sup> kg/(m·s)</span>, 18.1 μPa·s or <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">6995181000000000000♠</span>1.81<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>−5</sup> Pa·s</span>. The kinematic viscosity at 15 °C is <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">6995148000000000000♠</span>1.48<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>−5</sup> m<sup>2</sup>/s</span> or 14.8 cSt. At 25 °C, the viscosity is 18.6 μPa·s and the kinematic viscosity 15.7 cSt.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Viscosity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dynamic_Viscosity_of_Water.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="429" data-file-width="400" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Dynamic_Viscosity_of_Water.png/220px-Dynamic_Viscosity_of_Water.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Dynamic_Viscosity_of_Water.png/330px-Dynamic_Viscosity_of_Water.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6a/Dynamic_Viscosity_of_Water.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dynamic_Viscosity_of_Water.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dynamic viscosity of water</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dynamics_(mechanics)" title="Dynamics (mechanics)">dynamic</a> viscosity of <a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">water</a> is <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">6996890000000000000♠</span>8.90<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>−4</sup> <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">Pa</a>·<a href="/wiki/Second" title="Second">s</a></span> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">6997890000000000000♠</span>8.90<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>−3</sup> dyn·s/cm<sup>2</sup></span> or 0.890 cP at about 25 °C.
</p><p>As a function of temperature <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">T</span> (in kelvins): <span class="texhtml"><i>μ</i> = <i>A</i> × 10<sup><i>B</i>/(<i>T</i> − <i>C</i>)</sup></span>, where <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">A</span> = <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">6995241400000000000♠</span>2.414<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>−5</sup> Pa·s</span>, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">B</span> = 247.8 K, and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">C</span> = 140 K.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The dynamic viscosity of liquid water at different temperatures up to the normal boiling point is listed below.

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_substances">Other substances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Viscosity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Other substances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Drop_0.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1398" data-file-width="886" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Drop_0.jpg/170px-Drop_0.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Drop_0.jpg/255px-Drop_0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Drop_0.jpg/340px-Drop_0.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Drop_0.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Example of the viscosity of milk and water. <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Runny_hunny.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2700" data-file-width="1780" height="258" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Runny_hunny.jpg/170px-Runny_hunny.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Runny_hunny.jpg/255px-Runny_hunny.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Runny_hunny.jpg/340px-Runny_hunny.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Runny_hunny.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Honey" title="Honey">Honey</a> being drizzled</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PeanutButter.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="1141" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/PeanutButter.jpg/220px-PeanutButter.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/PeanutButter.jpg/330px-PeanutButter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/PeanutButter.jpg/440px-PeanutButter.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PeanutButter.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Peanut_butter" title="Peanut butter">Peanut butter</a> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-solid" title="Semi-solid">semi-solid</a> and can therefore hold peaks.</div></div></div>

<div class="mw-references-wrap"></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Blends_of_liquids">Blends of liquids</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Viscosity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Blends of liquids">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The viscosity of the blend of two or more liquids can be estimated using the Refutas equation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> The calculation is carried out in three steps.
</p><p>The first step is to calculate the viscosity blending number (VBN) (also called the viscosity blending index) of each component of the blend:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathrm {VBN} =14.534\times \ln {\big (}\ln(\nu +0.8){\big )}+10.975\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">V</mi>
<mi mathvariant="normal">B</mi>
<mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>14.534</mn>
<mo>×<!-- × --></mo>
<mi>ln</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo maxsize="1.2em" minsize="1.2em">(</mo>
</mrow>
</mrow>
<mi>ln</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>ν<!-- ν --></mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>0.8</mn>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo maxsize="1.2em" minsize="1.2em">)</mo>
</mrow>
</mrow>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>10.975</mn>
<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathrm {VBN} =14.534\times \ln {\big (}\ln(\nu +0.8){\big )}+10.975\,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathrm {VBN} =14.534\times \ln {\big (}\ln(\nu +0.8){\big )}+10.975\,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ef110677f98f928ac0994e2d11ab6d1efe57c534" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:42.853ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span> <span style="padding-left:3em;"> </span> (1)</dd></dl>
<p>where <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ν</span> is the kinematic viscosity in centistokes (cSt). It is important that the kinematic viscosity of each component of the blend be obtained at the same temperature.
</p><p>The next step is to calculate the VBN of the blend, using this equation:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathrm {VBN_{Blend}} =\left(x_{\mathrm {A} }\times \mathrm {VBN_{A}} \right)+\left(x_{\mathrm {B} }\times \mathrm {VBN_{B}} \right)+\cdots +\left(x_{\mathrm {N} }\times \mathrm {VBN_{N}} \right)\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathrm {VBN_{Blend}} =\left(x_{\mathrm {A} }\times \mathrm {VBN_{A}} \right)+\left(x_{\mathrm {B} }\times \mathrm {VBN_{B}} \right)+\cdots +\left(x_{\mathrm {N} }\times \mathrm {VBN_{N}} \right)\,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fa8d19368050044b9637a80554e89f015d8c881b" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:66.257ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> <span style="padding-left:3em;"> </span> (2)</dd></dl>
<p>where <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sub>X</sub></span> is the <a href="/wiki/Mass_fraction_(chemistry)" title="Mass fraction (chemistry)">mass fraction</a> of each component of the blend.

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Slurry">Slurry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Viscosity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Slurry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Slurry_Viscosity_Plot.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="554" data-file-width="778" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Slurry_Viscosity_Plot.png/300px-Slurry_Viscosity_Plot.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Slurry_Viscosity_Plot.png/450px-Slurry_Viscosity_Plot.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Slurry_Viscosity_Plot.png/600px-Slurry_Viscosity_Plot.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Slurry_Viscosity_Plot.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Plot of slurry relative viscosity <span class="texhtml"><i>μ</i><sub>r</sub></span> as calculated by empirical correlations from Einstein,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Einstein_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Einstein-50">[49]</a></sup> Guth and Simha,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuthAndSimha_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-GuthAndSimha-51">[50]</a></sup> Thomas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thomas_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas-52">[51]</a></sup> and Kitano <i>et al.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KitanoEtAl_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-KitanoEtAl-53">[52]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The term <a href="/wiki/Slurry" title="Slurry">slurry</a> describes mixtures of a liquid and solid particles that retain some fluidity. The viscosity of slurry can be described as relative to the viscosity of the liquid phase:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mu _{\mathrm {s} }=\mu _{\mathrm {r} }\mu _{\mathrm {l} },}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">s</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<msub>
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">r</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msub>
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mu _{\mathrm {s} }=\mu _{\mathrm {r} }\mu _{\mathrm {l} },}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mu _{\mathrm {s} }=\mu _{\mathrm {r} }\mu _{\mathrm {l} },}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5d649dc26803b4fa54017c21d75877a43fdd23ff" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:10.397ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>where <span class="texhtml"><i>μ</i><sub>s</sub></span> and <span class="texhtml"><i>μ</i><sub>l</sub></span> are respectively the dynamic viscosity of the slurry and liquid (Pa·s), and <span class="texhtml"><i>μ</i><sub>r</sub></span> is the <a href="/wiki/Relative_viscosity" title="Relative viscosity">relative viscosity</a> (dimensionless).
</p><p>Depending on the size and concentration of the solid particles, several models exist that describe the relative viscosity as a function of <a href="/wiki/Slurry#Volumetric_fraction_from_mass_fraction" title="Slurry">volume fraction</a> <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">φ</span> of solid particles.
</p><p>In the case of extremely low concentrations of fine particles, Einstein's equation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Einstein_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Einstein-50">[49]</a></sup> may be used:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mu _{\mathrm {r} }=1+2.5\varphi }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">r</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>2.5</mn>
<mi>φ<!-- φ --></mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mu _{\mathrm {r} }=1+2.5\varphi }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mu _{\mathrm {r} }=1+2.5\varphi }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2dba11dd07797d300b037b91d7032e202b2e04aa" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.872ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>In the case of higher concentrations, a modified equation was proposed by Guth and Simha,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuthAndSimha_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-GuthAndSimha-51">[50]</a></sup> which takes into account interaction between the solid particles:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mu _{\mathrm {r} }=1+2.5\varphi +14.1\varphi ^{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">r</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>2.5</mn>
<mi>φ<!-- φ --></mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>14.1</mn>
<msup>
<mi>φ<!-- φ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mu _{\mathrm {r} }=1+2.5\varphi +14.1\varphi ^{2}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mu _{\mathrm {r} }=1+2.5\varphi +14.1\varphi ^{2}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cf928fbe0a1c6332be0f2e5ee52854f72bfccce8" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:23.421ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Further modification of this equation was proposed by Thomas<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thomas_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas-52">[51]</a></sup> from the fitting of empirical data:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mu _{\mathrm {r} }=1+2.5\varphi +10.05\varphi ^{2}+Ae^{B\varphi },}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">r</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>2.5</mn>
<mi>φ<!-- φ --></mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>10.05</mn>
<msup>
<mi>φ<!-- φ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>A</mi>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nanofluids">Nanofluids</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Viscosity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Nanofluids">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AluminadasEthylene_Glycol.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="825" data-file-width="785" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/AluminadasEthylene_Glycol.tif/lossy-page1-220px-AluminadasEthylene_Glycol.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/AluminadasEthylene_Glycol.tif/lossy-page1-330px-AluminadasEthylene_Glycol.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/AluminadasEthylene_Glycol.tif/lossy-page1-440px-AluminadasEthylene_Glycol.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AluminadasEthylene_Glycol.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alumina-ethylene glycol, particle sizes 8 and 43 nm at 10 Celsius</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alumina-Ethylene_Glycol.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="825" data-file-width="785" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5e/Alumina-Ethylene_Glycol.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Alumina-Ethylene_Glycol.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5e/Alumina-Ethylene_Glycol.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Alumina-Ethylene_Glycol.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5e/Alumina-Ethylene_Glycol.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Alumina-Ethylene_Glycol.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alumina-Ethylene_Glycol.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Magnatite-water, particle sizes 25nm at 20 Celsius</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nanofluid" title="Nanofluid">Nanofluid</a> is a novel class of fluid, which is developed by dispersing nano-sized particles in base fluid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>Einstein model
</p><p>Einstein derived the applicable first theoretical formula for the estimation of viscosity values of composites or mixtures in 1906. This model developed while assuming linear viscous fluid including suspensions of rigid and spherical particles. Einstein’s model is valid for very low <a href="/wiki/Volume_fraction" title="Volume fraction">volume fraction</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \varnothing }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi class="MJX-variant">∅<!-- ∅ --></mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \varnothing }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\varnothing " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/00595c5e33692e724937fdcc8870496acce1ac74" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.808ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Einstein_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-Einstein-50">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mu _{nf}=\mu _{bf}(1+2.5\varnothing )}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Amorphous_materials">Amorphous materials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Viscosity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Amorphous materials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Glassviscosityexamples.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1972" data-file-width="2878" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Glassviscosityexamples.png/300px-Glassviscosityexamples.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Glassviscosityexamples.png/450px-Glassviscosityexamples.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Glassviscosityexamples.png/600px-Glassviscosityexamples.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Glassviscosityexamples.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Common <a href="/wiki/Glass" title="Glass">glass</a> viscosity curves<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Viscous flow in <a href="/wiki/Amorphous_solid" title="Amorphous solid">amorphous materials</a> (e.g. in <a href="/wiki/Glass" title="Glass">glasses</a> and melts)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> is a thermally activated process:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mu =Ae^{\frac {Q}{RT}},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>A</mi>
<msup>
<mi>e</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mi>Q</mi>
<mrow>
<mi>R</mi>
<mi>T</mi>
</mrow>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mu =Ae^{\frac {Q}{RT}},}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mu =Ae^{\frac {Q}{RT}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8cbac06ef814e1d443a99a481d2abcd663d640ea" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:10.994ex; height:4.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>where <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">Q</span> is activation energy, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">T</span> is temperature, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">R</span> is the molar gas constant and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">A</span> is approximately a constant.
</p><p>The viscous flow in amorphous materials is characterized by a deviation from the <a href="/wiki/Arrhenius_equation" title="Arrhenius equation">Arrhenius-type</a> behavior: <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">Q</span> changes from a high value <span class="texhtml"><i>Q</i><sub>H</sub></span> at low temperatures (in the glassy state) to a low value <span class="texhtml"><i>Q</i><sub>L</sub></span> at high temperatures (in the liquid state). Depending on this change, amorphous materials are classified as either
</p>
<ul><li>strong when: <span class="texhtml"><i>Q</i><sub>H</sub> − <i>Q</i><sub>L</sub> &lt; <i>Q</i><sub>L</sub></span> or</li>
<li>fragile when: <span class="texhtml"><i>Q</i><sub>H</sub> − <i>Q</i><sub>L</sub> ≥ <i>Q</i><sub>L</sub></span>.</li></ul>
<p>The fragility of amorphous materials is numerically characterized by Doremus' fragility ratio:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle R_{\mathrm {D} }={\frac {Q_{\mathrm {H} }}{Q_{\mathrm {L} }}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>R</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">D</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<msub>
<mi>Q</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">H</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msub>
<mi>Q</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">L</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle R_{\mathrm {D} }={\frac {Q_{\mathrm {H} }}{Q_{\mathrm {L} }}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle R_{\mathrm {D} }={\frac {Q_{\mathrm {H} }}{Q_{\mathrm {L} }}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f7532c0a03981d677e256c9185a1e57856eff6bb" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:10.49ex; height:5.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>and strong materials have <span class="texhtml"><i>R</i><sub>D</sub> &lt; 2</span> whereas fragile materials have <span class="texhtml"><i>R</i><sub>D</sub> ≥ 2</span>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:B2O3_viscosoty.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="627" data-file-width="939" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/B2O3_viscosoty.jpg/220px-B2O3_viscosoty.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/B2O3_viscosoty.jpg/330px-B2O3_viscosoty.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/B2O3_viscosoty.jpg/440px-B2O3_viscosoty.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:B2O3_viscosoty.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Common_logarithm" title="Common logarithm">Common logarithm</a> of viscosity against temperature for <a href="/wiki/Boron_trioxide" title="Boron trioxide">B<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub></a>, showing two regimes</div></div></div>
<p>The viscosity of amorphous materials is quite exactly described by a two-exponential equation:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mu =A_{1}T\left(1+A_{2}e^{\frac {B}{RT}}\right)\left(1+Ce^{\frac {D}{RT}}\right),}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<msub>
<mi>A</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mi>T</mi>
<mrow>
<mo>(</mo>
<mrow>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo>+</mo>
<msub>
<mi>A</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msup>
<mi>e</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mi>B</mi>
<mrow>
<mi>R</mi>
<mi>T</mi>
</mrow>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mrow>
<mo>)</mo>
</mrow>
<mrow>
<mo>(</mo>
<mrow>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>C</mi>
<msup>
<mi>e</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mi>D</mi>
<mrow>
<mi>R</mi>
<mi>T</mi>
</mrow>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mrow>
<mo>)</mo>
</mrow>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mu =A_{1}T\left(1+A_{2}e^{\frac {B}{RT}}\right)\left(1+Ce^{\frac {D}{RT}}\right),}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mu =A_{1}T\left(1+A_{2}e^{\frac {B}{RT}}\right)\left(1+Ce^{\frac {D}{RT}}\right),}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3bdba9ee2739b35716340c1f084a1b07a5ae1c8b" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:38.361ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>with constants <span class="texhtml"><i>A</i><sub>1</sub></span>, <span class="texhtml"><i>A</i><sub>2</sub></span>, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">B</span>, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">C</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">D</span> related to thermodynamic parameters of joining bonds of an amorphous material.
</p><p>Not very far from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glass_transition_temperature" title="Glass transition temperature">glass transition temperature</a>, <span class="texhtml"><i>T</i><sub>g</sub></span>, this equation can be approximated by a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Vogel-Fulcher-Tammann_equation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Vogel-Fulcher-Tammann equation (page does not exist)">Vogel–Fulcher–Tammann</a> (VFT) equation.
</p><p>If the temperature is significantly lower than the <a href="/wiki/Glass_transition" title="Glass transition">glass transition</a> temperature, <span class="texhtml"><i>T</i> ≪ <i>T</i><sub>g</sub></span>, then the two-exponential equation simplifies to an Arrhenius-type equation:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mu =A_{\mathrm {L} }Te^{\frac {Q_{\mathrm {H} }}{RT}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<msub>
<mi>A</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">L</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mi>T</mi>
<msup>
<mi>e</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<msub>
<mi>Q</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">H</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mrow>
<mi>R</mi>
<mi>T</mi>
</mrow>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mu =A_{\mathrm {L} }Te^{\frac {Q_{\mathrm {H} }}{RT}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mu =A_{\mathrm {L} }Te^{\frac {Q_{\mathrm {H} }}{RT}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9b226860d76ea64dbeba4221afb32703c52efbd2" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.48ex; height:4.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>with
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle Q_{\mathrm {H} }=H_{\mathrm {d} }+H_{\mathrm {m} },}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>Q</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">H</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<msub>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>+</mo>
<msub>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle Q_{\mathrm {H} }=H_{\mathrm {d} }+H_{\mathrm {m} },}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle Q_{\mathrm {H} }=H_{\mathrm {d} }+H_{\mathrm {m} },}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fefbbeb081e2cae33823bad418fe53607323b7e0" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:16.499ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>where <span class="texhtml"><i>H</i><sub>d</sub></span> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enthalpy_of_formation" title="Enthalpy of formation">enthalpy of formation</a> of broken bonds (termed configurons<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup>) and <span class="texhtml"><i>H</i><sub>m</sub></span> is the <a href="/wiki/Enthalpy" title="Enthalpy">enthalpy</a> of their motion.
</p><p>When the temperature is less than the glass transition temperature, <span class="texhtml"><i>T</i> &lt; <i>T</i><sub>g</sub></span>, the activation energy of viscosity is high because the amorphous materials are in the glassy state and most of their joining bonds are intact.
</p><p>If the temperature is much higher than the glass transition temperature, <span class="texhtml"><i>T</i> ≫ <i>T</i><sub>g</sub></span>, the two-exponential equation also simplifies to an Arrhenius-type equation:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mu =A_{\mathrm {H} }Te^{\frac {Q_{\mathrm {L} }}{RT}},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<msub>
<mi>A</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">H</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mi>T</mi>
<msup>
<mi>e</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<msub>
<mi>Q</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">L</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mrow>
<mi>R</mi>
<mi>T</mi>
</mrow>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mu =A_{\mathrm {H} }Te^{\frac {Q_{\mathrm {L} }}{RT}},}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mu =A_{\mathrm {H} }Te^{\frac {Q_{\mathrm {L} }}{RT}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7f1383d0c9a0068e033710d9bcef0eacd4380e25" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:14.166ex; height:4.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>with
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle Q_{\mathrm {L} }=H_{\mathrm {m} }.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>Q</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">L</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<msub>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle Q_{\mathrm {L} }=H_{\mathrm {m} }.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle Q_{\mathrm {L} }=H_{\mathrm {m} }.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0a09911ee79d38cc586bae4e0400db3f605697b8" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:10.376ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>When the temperature is higher than the glass transition temperature, <span class="texhtml"><i>T</i> &gt; <i>T</i><sub>g</sub></span>, the activation energy of viscosity is low because amorphous materials are melted and have most of their joining bonds broken, which facilitates flow.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Eddy_viscosity">Eddy viscosity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Viscosity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Eddy viscosity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the study of <a href="/wiki/Turbulence" title="Turbulence">turbulence</a> in <a href="/wiki/Fluid" title="Fluid">fluids</a>, a common practical strategy for calculation is to ignore the small-scale <a href="/wiki/Vortex" title="Vortex">vortices</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Eddy_(fluid_dynamics)" title="Eddy (fluid dynamics)">eddies</a>) in the motion and to calculate a large-scale motion with an eddy viscosity that characterizes the transport and dissipation of <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a> in the smaller-scale flow (see <a href="/wiki/Large_eddy_simulation" title="Large eddy simulation">large eddy simulation</a>). Values of eddy viscosity used in modeling <a href="/wiki/Ocean" title="Ocean">ocean</a> circulation may be from <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7004500000000000000♠</span>5<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>4</sup></span> to <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7006100000000000000♠</span>1<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>6</sup> Pa·s</span> depending upon the resolution of the numerical grid.
</p>
